14. DRAFTING WITH
DOCUMENT ASSEMBLY
PROGRAMS AND CLOSING
WITH ON LINE RESOURCES

T oday we are transitioning from a period when paper was king to a
          digital age when everything is recorded in computer files. When
          personal computers first became popular, attorneys used them to
replace a typewriter and a filing cabinet. But now more and more of the
actual drafting of documents is being done by computer. You don't need to
train yourself to work with every type of software, but you do need to know
what types of programs are out there and when they would be of use.
Beverly Rich, How AI is Changing Contracts, Harvard Business Review
(2018).

When I first started doing transactional work, it was common practice for
the closing attorney to deliver to the parties a "closing binder" after the
transaction was completed. The closing binder consisted of copies of all the
documents and a table of contents (a revised version of the closing agenda),
nicely "velo" bound together. Later the practice changed to providing the
same content on a computer disc (cd). Cd's save a lot of paper and space,
but there are also disadvantages to storing documents in digital form. CD's
replaced floppy disks which are now extinct. And CD's are being replaced
more and more by flash drives, so CD's may soon be extinct as well. I have
old files on my computer that I can no longer open because they were

                          Electronic copy available at: https://ssrn.com/abstract=4294001
drafted with software that is no longer in use. Say what you want about
paper and other primitive forms of storing information, but there are cave
paintings made by Neanderthals 64,000 years ago that you can still read.

A. Drafting with Document Assembly Programs

Today, computers are not only used to store documents, computers are also
used to draft documents. One type of program is just a form filler. The
user inputs factual information and the program inserts that information into
appropriate blanks in form documents. To use that type of program you
would first create a template for a document. Here is an example of what a
template for a short form mortgage might look like:

                                     MORTGAGE

         <<Borrower's Name>> of <<Borrower's Street Address>>,
 <<Borrower's County>> County, <<Borrower's State>>, for
 consideration paid, grants to <<Lender's Name >>of <<Lender's Street
 Address>>,<<Lender's County>> County, <<Lender's State>>, with
 MORTGAGE COVENANTS, to secure the payment of <<Amount of
 Loan in Words>> dollars in <<Term of Loan in Years>> years with
 <<Interest Rate in Percent>> per cent interest per annum, payable in
 <<Number of Installments>> installments, as provided in a promissory
 note of even date, the land together with the buildings thereon in
 <<Address of Mortgaged Property>>, <<County of Mortgaged
 Property>> County, <<State of Mortgaged Property>> more particularly
 described as follows:

                              <<Property Description>>

         This Mortgage is upon the STATUTORY CONDITION, for any
 breach of which Mortgagee shall have the STATUTORY POWER OF
 SALE.

         This Mortgage is executed under seal this ___ day of _________,
 ____.

                          Electronic copy available at: https://ssrn.com/abstract=4294001
        Mortgagor

        ___________________
        <<Borrower's Name>>

                COMMONWEALTH OF MASSACHUSETTS

<<County of Mortgaged Property>>

        On this ____ day of _________, ____, before me, personally
appeared <<Borrower's Name>>, who proved to me through satisfactory
evidence of identification, which was
___________________________________________________, to be the
persons whose name is signed on the preceding document, and
acknowledged to me that they signed it voluntarily for its stated purpose.

____________________________                                     _____
               Notary Public                                     My

commission expires:

You would next create an input screen you would use to enter the
information the software needs to fill out the document. That might look
like this:

                            Input Form for Mortgage
What is the borrower's name? __________________
What is the borrower street address?

Electronic copy available at: https://ssrn.com/abstract=4294001
        Street: _________________
        County: ________________
        State: __________________
What is the lender's name? ____________________
What is the lender's address?
        Street: __________________
        County: _________________
        State: ___________________
What is the amount of the loan in words? ______________________
dollars
What is the term of the loan? _________ years
What is the interest rate? ____________ percent
How many installments will there be? ___________
What is the address of the mortgaged property?

            Street: _________________
            County: ________________
            State: __________________
What is the legal description of the property?
___________________________________________________________
___________________________________________________________
___________________________________________________________
_________________________________________________________

                         Electronic copy available at: https://ssrn.com/abstract=4294001
Then you would enter the information into the input screen and the software
would produce a draft of the document based on the template.

Obviously you wouldn't go through all this trouble for just one short
document. You would use a program like this if you are repeatedly using
the same lengthy form documents for specific types of transactions. For
example, if your job is to conduct commercial loan closings for an
institutional client of the firm, and the client uses the same forms for each
transaction, then using a program like this to produce and initial draft of
documents for a deal would likely make the process much more efficient.

In addition, there are other programs you could use that are more
sophisticated. For example, there are programs that will not only fill in the
blanks, but also decide what types of provisions to use depending upon
what the facts are. So, the software might ask whether the loan is to be a
recourse loan or a nonrecourse loan. Depending upon the answer, the
software will insert the provisions applicable to a recourse loan or the
provisions applicable to a nonrecourse loan, and then fill in the blanks in
those provisions. The software might also ask for the identity of the
borrower. If the borrower is a partnership, then the program will add
provisions appropriate for a partnership. If the borrower is a corporation,
the program will add provisions appropriate for a corporation.

Banks use this kind of software to generate residential loan documents with
the usual Fannie Mae forms. Brokers use this type of software to generate
purchase and sale agreements and other simple documents for use in
residential real estate transactions. Similar programs are available to
consumers. Nolo sells a popular program called WillMaker that will walk a
non-lawyer through the process of drafting a last will and testament. Rocket
Lawyer, LegalZoom and Law Depot are online services that help consumers
and small businesses draft simple legal documents. Programs like
HotDocs, XpressDox, Contract Express and NetDocuments help lawyers to
produce a first draft of more complex documents. Also, some programs
interface with e-mail, filing and calendaring software, as well as client

                          Electronic copy available at: https://ssrn.com/abstract=4294001
websites. And programs like LegalSifter and LawGeex use artificial
intelligence to help attorneys review existing contracts. If I were in law
school today, I would consider learning how to use that type of software
and adding my proficiency with it to my resume.

Does all this mean we don't need lawyers? No. These programs make the
process more efficient, but they don't eliminate the need for good lawyers.
You should be aware of them because, as a practical matter, you have to be
able to do better than they can do. If the client can go online and print out a
document that is just as good as the one you drafted, then the client no
longer needs your services. It is more convenient, less expensive and less
time-consuming to have a computer draft a document than to meet with an
attorney and wait for the attorney to send you a draft (and a bill). As a
result, the product the attorney produces must always be better than any
computer can do.

                          Electronic copy available at: https://ssrn.com/abstract=4294001
                                B. Closing with Online Resources

                                           It also used to be that documents were executed in a closing in an
                                           attorney's office, but that is changing too. More and more
                                           documents are executed online with electronic signatures. For
                                           example, programs called DocuSign, DotLoop and HelloSign
                                           enable attorneys to have some real estate documents signed
                                           online. And some programs also facilitate the exchange of
document drafts and collaboration by attorneys.

Electronic signatures are governed by two statutes. The federal Electronic
Signatures in Global and National Commerce Act 15 U.S.C. §§7001-7031
declares that "a signature, contract, or other record relating to such
transaction may not be denied legal effect, validity, or enforceability solely
because it is in electronic form...." §7001(a)(1). The Uniform Electronic
Transactions Act, a uniform state law, similarly declares the validity and
enforceability of electronic signatures. In Florida, the law specifically
provides as follows:

 LEGAL RECOGNITION OF ELECTRONIC RECORDS,
 ELECTRONIC SIGNATURES, AND ELECTRONIC CONTRACTS.--

 (a)A record or signature may not be denied legal effect or
 enforceability solely because the record or signature is in electronic form.
 (b)A contract may not be denied legal effect or enforceability solely
 because an electronic record was used in the formation of the contract.
 (c)If a provision of law requires a record to be in writing, an electronic
 record satisfies such provision.
 (d)If a provision of law requires a signature, an electronic signature
 satisfies such provision.

 Fla. Stat. §668.50(7).

Someday we may find ourselves relying on a retinal scan or some other biometric measure to show
that an agreement was made. Suraiya Jabin & Farhana Zareen, Biometric Signature Verification,
International Journal of Biometrics (January 2015). For now it is often still necessary that a deed be
signed in person, on paper, and in the presence of a notary for a real estate closing to occur. And

                          Electronic copy available at: https://ssrn.com/abstract=4294001
banks still typically insist that their loan documents be signed in person. So, attorneys still conduct
in person closings, although they may happen less often.

C. Smart Contracts

In addition to contracts being drafted by computer programs and
agreements being signed online, contracts are also being performed by
computers on line as well. An example of that is a so called "smart
contract."

A smart contract is a computer program that is part of a block chain. The
block chain is a series of connected programs that allow users to transfer
payments on line without an intermediary. A smart contract works by
following one or more "if/ then..." statements that are written into the
program. The purpose of a smart contract is to provide a mechanism for
transactions to occur, like a transfer of digital currency, or an exchange of
digital currency for a digital asset, when certain conditions are met and
without the need for a third party. The Etherium block chain is the most
popular block chain for smart contracts; the programming language most
commonly used for smart contracts is Solidity.

"Crowdfunding" is an example of a smart contract used to transfer digital
currency. The contract initially serves to secure funds from investors for a
project. If a predetermined level of investment is reached, the contract
automatically transfers the funds to the creators for the project. If the level
of investment is not reached, the funds are returned to the investors.

OpenSea.com is another example of smart contract technology. On that
platform consumers and content creators can buy and sell various Non-
Fungible Tokens (digital assets) like music and photography. The NFT's
are paid for with digital currencies in a buyer's virtual wallet (MetaMask,
Coinbase Wallet, TrustWallet, etc.)

There are two types of smart contracts: deterministic and non-
deterministic. A deterministic smart contract gets the information it needs
to execute a transaction from the block chain. A non-deterministic smart
contract requires information outside the block chain to operate. Non-
deterministic contracts require the involvement of an oracle, which creates a

                          Electronic copy available at: https://ssrn.com/abstract=4294001
link between the contract and the real world. The purpose of an oracle is to
retrieve and verify external information for a smart contract. An example
would be market data from an external feed.

You could think of a purchase and sale agreement as a transaction subject to
a series of conditions. The primary condition for delivery of the subject
matter is the purchase price. Real estate and goods are not digital assets,
but the transfer of ownership could be memorialized in a deed or bill of
sale, and either of those documents could be converted to digital form. The
real problem, however, is that many of the conditions to a typical purchase
and sale arrangement are external to the block chain and would have to be
retrieved and verified not by an oracle but either by the parties themselves
or by one or more third parties involved in the transaction. Until that
problem is solved, smart contracts will primarily serve as a mechanism for
making payments with digital currencies, and buying and selling NFT's.

Attorneys are using technology more and more, just like everyone else. But
in the most important respects, the attorney's role remains unchanged.
When you represent a client, the client is not paying you to obtain a form
document or fill in the blanks and print one out, and then witness your
signature. The client is paying you to think. It is important that you have
the skill to express the client's agreement in a clear, complete, and accurate
manner. But substance is what matters most. And that means using the
knowledge and training you began to acquire in law school and continued
to build on in practice to advance the client's goals and protect the client's
interests. Computers may make the process more efficient. But until the
day comes when a computer can go through law school and think like a
lawyer, there will always be a need for the minds of people like us. There
will always be a place for smart, knowledgeable lawyers who draft well.

                                  Practice Exercises

         Create a sample template and input form for the Associate
 Employment Agreement, Laptop Purchase Agreement, Residential Lease

                          Electronic copy available at: https://ssrn.com/abstract=4294001
Agreement, Sale of Assets Agreement and/or Consulting Services
Agreement you drafted as the practice exercises for the previous chapters.

15. DRAFTING A CONTRACT
AMENDMENT

T here is one more skill that I think is important to know if you are
          going to practice in this area, and that is how to draft a contract
          amendment. For a variety of reasons, you may need to go back
and change something in a contract you have already drafted. One party or
the other may have changed their practices. Something about the way the
deal was originally planned may not be working as well as it could. Or, the
parties may want to expand what they had originally contemplated doing.
When this happens, drafting a new agreement may be an option. But often
the preferred method is to leave what already exists in place and just
provide for the new terms. If you need to draft a contract amendment, here
is a quick outline of how to do it.

The first thing you need to think about when drafting an amendment is
whether it is better to amend the document or just start over with a new
agreement. The one big advantage of amending is it doesn't give the other
party an opportunity to renegotiate any of the provisions that aren't
changing. But there are other legal issues to consider as well. If the
document is a security instrument, the client may lose the priority of their
interest by starting over. So, it may be better to amend. If the document is
a negotiable instrument, amending may destroy the negotiability of the
instrument. So, it may be better to start over and re-do the original
document. Consider those issues first. If an amendment makes sense, then
start drafting.

                          Electronic copy available at: https://ssrn.com/abstract=4294001
Start off with a title and exordium, referring to the original agreement, like
this:

                  AMENDMENT TO APARTMENT LEASE

 This Amendment to Apartment Lease (Amendment) dated January
 25, 2019, is by and between South Tower Management Corp., a
 Florida Corporation having an office at 123 Main Street in
 Jacksonville, Florida (Landlord) and William Lancaster III, an
 individual having a residence at 23 Beach Avenue, Apt. 567,
 Jacksonville Beach, Florida (Tenant). The parties mutually agree as
 follows:

Then draft a background section explaining what happened and why the
parties are amending the original document.

 1. Background of Amendment

 A. On January 2, 2015 Landlord and Tenant entered into an
 apartment lease for the property located at 31 West Street, Unit 310,
 Gainesville, Florida (the Lease).

 B. The Lease was for a term of four (4) years beginning on
 January 2, 2015 and ending on January 1, 2019; and the monthly rent
 provided for in the Lease was $1,500 per month.

 C. The Tenant now desires to extend the term of the Lease; and
 the Landlord is willing to extend the term at a higher rental rate.

 Accordingly, the parties mutually agree as follows:

If you want to use the defined terms in the original lease, then consider
adding a statement like this: "Capitalized terms not otherwise defined in

                          Electronic copy available at: https://ssrn.com/abstract=4294001
this Amendment have the same meanings as provided in the Lease."
After you have completed the background section, explain what each
change is, as though you are editing the original document. In other words,
reference the section to change, delete the old language, and insert the new
language, like this:

 2. Changes to Lease
 A. Section 3 of the Lease (Term of Rental) is deleted and replaced
 with the following:

        "3. Term of Rental
        The term of the rental is for four (4) years beginning on
 January 2, 2019 and ending on January 1, 2023."
 B. Section 4(a) of the Lease (Payment of Rent) is deleted and
 replaced with the following:
        "(a) Payment of Rent
        On or before the first day of each month, the Tenant will pay
 the Landlord rent in the amount of two thousand dollars ($2,000) per
 month."

Once you have made all the changes, finish with a reiteration of the rest of
the contract, a testimonium, and signature lines.

 3. Remainder of Lease
 All other terms and conditions of the Lease remain in full force and
 effect.

                          Electronic copy available at: https://ssrn.com/abstract=4294001
Executed by the parties as of the date above.

Landlord                Tenant

_________________           _________________
South Tower Mgmt Corp.  William Lancaster III
By: [Name] [Title]

Now you know how to draft a contract from scratch, revise a form
document, negotiate terms, and close a deal. And you also know how to
amend a contract after the deal is done. That is pretty much everything you
need to know to start drafting contracts and practicing as a transactional
lawyer.

Keep learning as much as you can; and seek perfection in everything you
write. Good luck!

FLOWCHART FOR DRAFTING
CONTRACT PROVISIONS

                          Electronic copy available at: https://ssrn.com/abstract=4294001
Electronic copy available at: https://ssrn.com/abstract=4294001
Electronic copy available at: https://ssrn.com/abstract=4294001
Electronic copy available at: https://ssrn.com/abstract=4294001
CONTRACT DRAFTING
CHECKLIST

1. Begin your provisions with the name of a party, not a non-party or a
thing.
2. Use "shall" or "will" to obligate the party to act.
3. Use "shall not" or "will not" to prohibit the party from acting.
4. Use "may" to give the party the right to act.
5. Don't use any other words for obligations, prohibitions or rights. (i.e.
don't use "agrees," "has discretion," "is prohibited," "is required to," etc.).
6. Draft descriptions as past or present tense statements. There is seldom a
need to use future tense in an agreement.
7. Make the subject of sentences the relevant party; use active voice.
8. Make sentences complete (state who, what, to whom, when and how, if
applicable).
9. Omit legalese and other needless jargon.
10. Proofread for spelling, punctuation, and grammar.
11. Start with a Title identifying the type of contract.
12. Then an Exordium containing the following information

                          Electronic copy available at: https://ssrn.com/abstract=4294001
(Don't give this section a heading): effective date, name of parties, address
and state of organization, if applicable, reference to title, and expression of
intent to be bound by the contract's provisions.

13. Use short forms to refer to the parties and the agreement (put in
parenthesis; start with a capital letter).

14. Use a heading for each subsequent section of contract (except for the
testimonium and the signature lines at the end); subsections should also
have headings. Each heading and subsection should be numbered or
lettered, if there is more than one.

15. Draft a Background of Agreement section, if applicable. Recite
business or nature of parties, history and reasons for transaction, or
description of subject matter. Use descriptive statements.

16. Draft the Core Obligations. Obligate each side to complete their part of
the bargain; express the core exchange of promises between the parties.
(Don't label this section "Core Obligations," Do use "will" or "shall").

17. Draft Duration, if applicable. Describe the intended length of the period
and state the beginning and ending dates.

18. Draft Supplemental Provisions for the details of the agreement. Expand
upon the services to be provided and payments to be made; express the
details of when, where, and how. (Don't label this section "Supplemental
Provisions" or "Obligations of X" and "Obligations of Y;" Do use "will,"
"shall" or "may").

19. Payment Clauses. Indicate who payment is to, when it is due, how it is
to be made, and what payment is for.

20. Time Clauses. Use "on" for due dates, "before," "on or before," "after,"
"on or after," "no later than," or "no earlier than" for deadlines. Make sure
the "trigger date" is clear. Use days instead of weeks or months.

21. Conditions. Use "if," "unless," or "except." If a time clause modifies a
condition, place the time clause within the phrase of the condition the time
clause refers to.

                          Electronic copy available at: https://ssrn.com/abstract=4294001
22. Insurance. Use "will maintain" or "shall maintain." Identify the type of
insurance and amount of coverage. Name the other party as beneficiary /
loss payee. Require the party to provide proof of insurance.
23. Indemnity. Use "will" or "shall." Identify the person the clause applies
to. Specify the items indemnified. Indicate if negligence and attorney's
fees are included. State any exceptions.
24. Termination / Cancellation. Use "may." Cancellation if breach;
otherwise termination. Specify method of termination.
25. Modification. Descriptive policy that modifications are valid only if
done with a written record signed by all parties.
26. Integration / Merger. Describe the parol evidence rule. Contract is
integrated, complete, and final. Prior agreements are merged, superseded.
27. Forum Selection / Venue. Describe forum choice. Make the clause
mandatory and exclusive. Make the clause conspicuous. Delineate the
scope of the clause.
28. Applicable Law. Describe choice for applicable law. State what law
applies to determine the scope of the choice of law clause. State what law
applies to a claim based on a tort or statute.
29. Testimonium. "Executed by the parties as of the date written above."
Do not use legalese. (Do not give this section a heading).
30. Signature Lines. Include the name for an individual (personal liability);
"by," "name," and "title" if a representative (no personal liability).

                          Electronic copy available at: https://ssrn.com/abstract=4294001
DRAFTING EXERCISES

       M E M O R A N D U M

To:    ________________

From:  ________________

Date:  ________________

Subject: Associate Employment Agreement

_____________________________________________________________
_________________

Welcome to Big Law, LLP. I have a project I would like you to start
working on a.s.a.p. As you know, Big Law hires the best and the brightest
law students from the top law schools in Florida. Big Law is a limited
liability partnership located at 456 Gulf Shore Boulevard in Naples,
Florida. We are a large general practice firm, and employ approximately
300 lawyers.

Every year, Big Law interviews students at top Florida law schools, then
does call back interviews at the firm for a small group of highly qualified
applicants. Right now, we are hiring about a dozen associates per year, but
that may change depending upon market conditions.

Although the firm's associates have historically been employees at will, Big
Law would like to make the firm more marketable to prospective associates

       Electronic copy available at: https://ssrn.com/abstract=4294001
by offering them written contracts. And we would like your help drafting a
form document we can use.

The agreement will be for a one-year term, renewable at the end of each
year at our option (not the associate's option). We will let the associate
know three months before the end of the term. The employer should be Big
Law; and you will need to insert blanks for the employee, a law student
residing in Florida.

We think it is important to make clear in the agreement we rely on the
veracity of the statements in each candidate's resume. If any of those
statements turn out to be false, we would want the right to end the
relationship. And we would also want the right to do that if the candidate
either fails to graduate from law school or fails to pass the bar exam (or is
subsequently disbarred).

As you know, we pay our associates well. The starting salary is $160,000
per year (payable every other week). We provide full health insurance
coverage, dental and vision insurance for the associate and his or her family,
as well as a life insurance policy in the amount of $250,000. Also, we
make matching contributions to a 401(k) plan of up to six percent of the
associate's salary.

Big law agrees to reimburse associates for their yearly license fee and the
cost of attendance at continuing legal education conferences within the
associate's area(s) of expertise or for approved legal ethics, bias
elimination, substance abuse, or mental illness awareness programs, or
professionalism programs.

We do not require our associates to reimburse the firm for damages caused
by them as a result of their negligence. But we do require associates to
reimburse the firm for uninsured losses caused by the associate's gross
negligence or willful misconduct. (Uninsured losses may occur either
because the relevant conduct isn't covered or because it is covered but a
deductible applies to a portion of the loss.)

                          Electronic copy available at: https://ssrn.com/abstract=4294001
In exchange we require all associates to work a minimum of 1,800 billable
hours per year. Time is billable only if it is spent working on a specific
matter for a client of the firm. Associates must keep track of their time
every day and submit daily timesheets to their administrative assistant.

Clients of the firm must always be represented by associates in a competent,
professional and ethical manner, in accordance with prevailing standards of
legal practice. Also, associates are required to attend periodic department
meetings and other firm events, and comply with any ethical requirements
for continuing legal education.

As long as each associate meets the billable hour's requirement, the
associate is welcome to take up to four weeks' vacation. And, as long as
that requirement is met, he or she can do as much pro bono work as he or
she desires. However, the associate must inform the firm of the pro bono
work and arrange for a partner of the firm to provide supervision for the
work.

It should also be made clear, however, that time spent completing
administrative tasks, attending continuing legal education classes, working
on pro bono cases, and other matters not billable to a firm client for a
specific matter is not included in the billable hour's requirement.

In addition, we require associates to devote all of their professional time,
attention and energies to the business of Law Firm (e.g. an associate cannot
work at the firm and also have their own practice on the side). Here is a
sample provision I found in an employment agreement for a pharmacist
(you will have to fix the language):

        Fidelity. The Agent agrees to devote all of the Agent's
        professional time, attention and energies to the
        pharmaceutical business of the hereinbefore mentioned
        Corporation. During the term of this contract, said Agent
        may not at any time hereafter engage in the practice of
        pharmacy to any extent whatsoever, except pursuant to this
        arrangement with the Corporation.

                          Electronic copy available at: https://ssrn.com/abstract=4294001
The firm expects associates to act in an appropriate manner at all times, and
not engage in any conduct that would hurt the firm's reputation.
Discrimination against employees of the firm on the basis of race or gender,
and sexual harassment will not be tolerated and will also be grounds for
dismissal. Here is another sample provision I found in an employment
agreement for a realtor (again, you will have to fix the language).

        Conduct. Any conduct that might injure the professional
        reputation and standing of Employer in the real estate
        brokerage community shall not hereafter be engaged in by the
        Employee. Discrimination against brokers, salesmen and
        other employees of the Employer, on the basis of race or
        gender also may not be engaged in by aforementioned
        Employee; and said employee must not sexually harass
        employees of said Employer.

We review each associate's performance in a yearly evaluation. If the
associate's performance is satisfactory to us and the associate's services are
still needed by the firm, then we would want to have the right to renew the
contract for an additional year. If not, then we would want to have the right
to end the associate's employment.

If an associate desires to leave the firm, he or she must give us at least thirty
days' written notice. Associates are not permitted to solicit business from
any client of the firm for a period of one year after they leave, regardless of
whether the employee resigns or is terminated. Also, the identities of the
firm's clients and the matters in which we represent them have to be kept
confidential.

Please add the usual administrative provisions at the end of the agreement.
Agreements not included in the final document will be superseded. Oral
modifications after the agreement is signed will not be valid. Florida law
will be applied. If there is a dispute, the parties have to try mediation to
resolve it first (we agree to pay the cost). If that doesn't work, then any
lawsuits should be brought in the county the firm is located in.

Thank you in advance for your assistance.

                          Electronic copy available at: https://ssrn.com/abstract=4294001
TRANSCRIPT OF CLIENT
INTAKE FOR LAPTOP
PURCHASE AGREEMENT

Rodriguez: Good morning.

Lancaster: Good morning, Ben. How are you?

Rodriguez: I am well, Margaret. Thank you.

Lancaster: So, what brings you in today?

Rodriguez: Well, I've been working on an agreement with Apple
computer. I want you to document it.

Lancaster: Wonderful. Is the agreement with the University or just the

Law School? Rodriguez:    I think it should be with the Levin College

of Law.

Lancaster: We've worked with Apple before. I think the legal name is
"Apple, Inc." and they are out of California, right?

Rodriguez: Yes, they are a Delaware corporation located in California.
The address is One Apple Park Way in Cupertino.

Lancaster: I've been there. The giant circular building?

Rodriguez: That's it. Anyway, we went there to work with Apple to
address a student / teacher issue we've been dealing with. Students like to

         Electronic copy available at: https://ssrn.com/abstract=4294001
use laptops in class, but teachers find them distracting. Many of the law
school professors have outright banned them.

Lancaster: I see the issue. But it's not really the computer that is the
problem; it is the internet, right?
Rodriguez: Exactly. As it turns out, Apple has people working on the
same issue: making a classroom-friendly computer product. You know,
Apple has a lot of interest in education and working with teachers to
assimilate computers into the classroom.

Lancaster: I know. So, did you come up with a solution?

Rodriguez: I think so. Apple is going to develop a line of classroom
approved computers for us, and we are going to give them to all the
entering 1L students.
Lancaster: Wow. A free laptop for every student. Sounds like a good
marketing idea.

Rodriguez: It is, isn't it? We'll raise the tuition $1,000 to compensate, but
that's another issue.

Lancaster: So, what is a classroom approved computer?
Rodriguez: Well, it's basically the MacBook Air model with certain
modifications.

Lancaster: How is it different?

Rodriguez: First and foremost, it is Wi-fi and Bluetooth disabled. In other
words, it doesn't have either of those features, and it is made so neither can
be added. That's important, so we want them to put in writing in the
contract that these computers cannot be used for internet access.
Lancaster: I guess that takes care of internet surfing and e-mailing in
class.

                          Electronic copy available at: https://ssrn.com/abstract=4294001
Rodriguez: Right. Second, it is preloaded with E-books for all required
courses. We've already given the books to Apple, so they can upload them
to each laptop.

Lancaster: What a great idea. No more lugging around a backpack full of
books. The students will love that.

Rodriguez: Third, in terms of software, the laptops will also come with

Lancaster: Do they have to be set up or prepped or anything before the

         I need your help drafting a residential lease. As part of its efforts to
rise in prominence and the US News and World Report rankings, the
University of Florida has hired Harvard Professor, Dr. Cornel West as a
visiting professor for the next academic year. Dr. West will teach two
courses at UF next year, and he will also do a number of public speaking
engagements at the school.

            While Dr. West is in Gainesville, he will be renting the Powell
University House at 2151 W University Ave, Gainesville, FL 32603. UF
has been using the Powell House for alumni events, but recently converted
the building back to a residence for prominent visiting faculty. The house

          Electronic copy available at: https://ssrn.com/abstract=4294001
has five bedrooms and three bathrooms. It is 4,345 square feet and includes
a pool in the back yard. I need you to draft a lease for the rental of that
space by Dr. West.

            At the outset, I want to make clear that we do not want to use a
form lease or any canned rental provisions for this contract. The
relationship between the University and Dr. Cornel is not the usual
relationship between a landlord and tenant. Among other things, the school
is not renting the space for a profit and it is not in the business of renting
such space. Dr. West is a guest of the school, and UF wants to make sure he
is well taken care of while he is living in Gainesville.

            What I am looking for then is a readable document that sets forth
the arrangement between the parties in a clear and concise way. Don't
include any legalese. Use active voice and keep your sentences short and
simple. Use what you learned in your legal drafting class and draft the
lease from scratch.

            The owner of the Powell House is the University Housing Corp.,
a Florida corporation. Use 210 Gerson Hall P.O. Box 117166, Gainesville,
FL 32611-7166 as the address for the corporation, and the address for the
Powell University House as Dr. West's address.

         The parties agreed that the lease will be for ten months starting on
August 1st and ending on May 31st; and the rent will be $1,500 per month
due on the first day of the month.

         The house will be fully furnished. In fact, there are a number of
very expensive antiques in the Powell House, so we will need $1,500
security deposit. If either the building or the furniture is damaged, we
should be able to use the deposit money to cover the cost to repair or
replace the applicable items. And we'll give the remaining balance back
after the end of the term. If the damages exceed the amount of the deposit,
it should be clear the excess will have to be paid by Dr. Cornel on demand.
Also, with regard to the deposit, please make sure the lease complies with
Fla. Stat. sec. 83.49. But don't worry about any other legal requirements
for leases in Florida.

                          Electronic copy available at: https://ssrn.com/abstract=4294001
            UF agrees to take care of the maintenance for the outside of the
house, like cleaning the pool, spraying for bugs and keeping the lawn
mowed. We will probably be there once a week but don't put that in the
lease. Just say we'll do the maintenance. If more is needed, Dr. Cornell has
to let us know.

         UF pays the taxes on the Powell House and plans to obtain hazard
insurance for the house. If Dr. West gets a tax bill, he must send it to us
within a few days. Also, Dr. West has agreed to pay the premium for the
insurance, and he won't engage in any activities that would result in a
premium increase.

         Dr. West has also agreed to maintain the inside of the house and
keep it clean and sanitary. He knows there are valuable antiques inside, and
he will make reasonable efforts to protect them from damage. Pets are not
allowed; and smoking is not allowed either.

         I think it goes without saying, but let's make it clear anyway, Dr.
West can't make any alterations to the inside of the house without the
written consent of UF. And that includes painting the walls, putting
pictures or paintings up, or taking down what is already hanging.

            As with any lease, the landlord, UF should have the right to make
periodic inspections of the house. But the university won't do that unless
the inspections are during the week between the hours of 9:00 and 5:00 pm.
Also, the university has agreed to give Dr. West at least a week's notice in
advance of any inspection. And the notice will be provided in writing,
since Dr. West is notorious for not reading e-mails.

            The plan is for Dr. West to teach during the fall and spring
semesters, but there is a possibility he may stay an additional year. So he
should have the ability to renew for an additional year, if his tenure as
visiting professor is extended. To do that he should give UF written notice
at least a month before the lease ends. Also, if for any reason Dr. West is
not happy or otherwise wants to end the lease, he should be able to do so.
UF only requires that it be given at least one month's notice, in writing.

                          Electronic copy available at: https://ssrn.com/abstract=4294001
            If there are any problems with Dr. West not paying the rent on
time, UF will work to resolve the issue without any penalties being
imposed. So there should be no late fees, and costs of collection need not
be included. If any payment is not received, the University is going to send
Dr. West a written notice, reminding him the rent is due, and he will have
two weeks after he receives the notice to rectify the situation by making the
payment. Only if the payment is still not received after the notice and two
week period can the University terminate the lease and pursue legal action,
if necessary.

            There are some "boilerplate" provisions you should be sure to
include. We don't want Dr. West to be able to assign his interests in the
lease or sublet any of the space. We should make clear that "time is of the
essence." Also, any lawsuits should be brought in Alachua County, and the
law that applies should be Florida.

            W. Kent Fuchs will be signing the lease for the school and,
obviously, Dr. West will sign for himself. I think that's it. If you have any
questions, please do not hesitate to contact me.

            Thanks in advance for your help.

no legal proceedings pending against Coffee Castle that would affect the

equipment be taken off the market and not shown to any other prospective

Castle used). Bagel World has already signed a lease with the school,
renting the space as of the closing date for this transaction. Bagel World
has not yet decided if it will use the name "Bagel World" for the business.
That is not a concern for Coffee Castle, as long as Bagel World does not use
the name "Coffee Castle."

         The agreement should make clear prior statements and
understandings are not enforceable unless memorialized in the contract.
Subsequent agreements are also invalid unless reduced to writing and
signed by the parties. Florida law will govern the interpretation of the
agreement. If there is a lawsuit, the parties agree it will be commenced in
Alachua County. Those are all standard "boilerplate" provisions.

         I think that's it for now. Please have a draft on my desk by
morning. Thank you for your assistance.

INTRODUCTION TO
COMMERCIAL REAL ESTATE
LOAN DOCUMENTS

O ne of the most common areas of practice for transactional
            lawyers is commercial real estate lending. The documents that
            are typically used for that type of transaction are a promissory
note, guaranty, loan agreement, real estate mortgage and security
agreement. Needless to say, it is exceedingly unlikely that you would ever
be asked to draft those documents from scratch. If you need to develop
your own set of forms, you will likely do that by looking at precedent
language in other documents. More often, the firm you are working for or
the institutional client you represent will have their own set of documents
they will want you to use. So your job will be to tailor those documents to
the terms of the deal you are handling. To do that you will need a solid
understanding of what those documents are and why they are used to
protect a lender's interests in a commercial real estate transaction.

A. Promissory Note

A promissory note contains the borrower's promise to repay the loan. To
understand why promissory notes are drafted the way they are you have to
first have a basic understanding of the business of banking. From a bank's
perspective, the character of a financial transaction is the opposite of what it
is from the customer's perspective. When you deposit money with a bank,
you create a liability for the bank. Effectively, you are making a demand

                          Electronic copy available at: https://ssrn.com/abstract=4294001
loan to the bank for the amount of the deposit. Similarly, when you borrow
money from the bank, you are effectively creating an asset for the bank.
From the bank's perspective a loan is an asset, just like a corporate bond,
except the issuer is the bank's customer not a corporation. On the books of
the bank, deposits are liabilities and loans are assets.

Because a promissory note evidences an asset, it is important that the bank
be able to sell or transfer it to other banks or outside investors. Typically
bank loans are pooled in the secondary market and then securitized to
enable investors to invest in the pool of loans, just like investors invest in
groups of stocks by investing in a mutual fund. To facilitate that process,
promissory notes are usually drafted to qualify as negotiable instruments
under Article III of the Uniform Commercial Code.

A negotiable instrument is typically defined as "an unconditional promise
or order to pay a fixed amount of money, with or without interest or other
charges" that is (1) payable to bearer or to order, (2) payable on demand or
at a definite time; and (3) contains no other undertakings in addition to the
payment of money, except an undertaking or power to give collateral to
secure payment, an authorization or power to the holder to confess
judgment or realize on or dispose of collateral; or a waiver of the benefit of
any law intended for the advantage or protection of an obligor. E.g., Fla.
Stat. § 673.1041.

For these reasons, promissory notes are typically very simple and short.
There is no exordium and no background section. The body of the
document is usually just the core obligation (the promise to repay the loan).
Rather than using "will," the obligation is often drafted with "promises to."
Also, to comply with Article III, it is made clear that the payee is not simply
the lender, but rather "to the order of" the lender.

         For value received, the undersigned ________________, a
 _____________ corporation, with an address of
 _________________________ (the "Borrower"), promises to pay to the
 order of __________ Bank, a _________________ Bank with an address

                          Electronic copy available at: https://ssrn.com/abstract=4294001
 of __________________________________ (together with its successors
 and assigns, the "Lender"), the principal amount of _______________
 Thousand Dollars and Zero Cents ($____,000.00) on or before
 ___________ __, ____ (the "Maturity Date"), as set forth below, together
 with interest from the date hereof on the unpaid principal balance from
 time to time outstanding until paid in full.

Next the interest rate and the due date for monthly payments are typically
set forth.

         The aggregate principal balance outstanding shall bear interest
 thereon at a per annum rate equal to ___________ Percent (____%). All
 accrued and unpaid interest shall be payable monthly in arrears on the 1st
 of each month, commencing on _____________, providing that, in any
 event, on the Maturity Date all outstanding principal, plus interest thereon
 and all costs and expenses, shall be due and payable.

And that's pretty much it. Often there is added a provision for late fees in
the event of late payment, and the recovery of attorney's fees, if the loan
goes into collection. The waivers referred to in the UCC are included (e.g.,
diligence, presentment, protest and demand, and notice of protest of
demand, of non-payment, of dishonor and of maturity). And there may be
one administrative provision (typically just choice of law). But otherwise,
there are just the testimonium and signature lines. Notably, a promissory
note is only signed by one party: the borrower.

B. Guaranty

A guaranty is a document in which someone other than the borrower
guarantees the borrower's obligation to repay the loan in the even the
borrower fails to pay. A guaranty is also a short, simple document, and it is
usually organized like a promissory note. A guaranty consists primarily of
the core obligation (the guarantors agreement to pay the borrower's debt in

                          Electronic copy available at: https://ssrn.com/abstract=4294001
the event that the borrower defaults on the loan obligation). Oddly, the
lender is often referred to as "you" in a guaranty.

         To induce you to make or continue to make loans or advances, or
 grant other financial accommodations to _____________________, a
 ____________ corporation, having an address at
 ______________________ ("Borrower"), pursuant to a Promissory Note
 in the original principal sum of $___,000.00, of even date herewith, and
 all other documents executed in connection therewith (collectively, the
 "Loan Documents") and in consideration thereof, the undersigned
 Guarantor guarantees the payment to you of all sums which may be
 presently due and owing and of all sums which shall in the future become
 due and owing to you from the Borrower under said Loan Documents,
 and also guarantees the due performance by the Borrower of all its
 obligations under said Loan Documents.

As with a promissory note, various waivers are often added to the
document. And then the document typically ends with just one signature:
that of the guarantor.

C. Loan Agreement

A loan agreement contains all the other agreements and representations
between the borrower and the bank. Like the other agreements I have
discussed in this book, a loan agreement typically starts off with an
exordium, background section and definitions.

If the loan is for the construction of the property, then the loan agreement
will next include the conditions to making the loan and funding each
advance. The conditions to making the loan include what is normally
produced at the loan closing, like execution of the loan documents and the
delivery of legal opinions. The conditions to each advance often include
the borrower's submission of a request in the required form as well as the
bank's inspection and approval of whatever work has been done. Also,
there is usually an "in balance" provision requiring that the remaining

                          Electronic copy available at: https://ssrn.com/abstract=4294001
proceeds of the loan provide sufficient funds to complete and operate the
project. Here is a brief example:

 (C) The Lender may require as a condition of any advance that the
 Borrower submit satisfactory evidence that the unadvanced portions of
 the Loan and the Construction Financing are sufficient to pay all costs for
 the completion of the Project in accordance with the Project Budget and
 the approved plans and specifications.

Whether the loan is for construction or acquisition, various representations
and warranties will be listed next. These represent the assumptions upon
which the decision to lend was based and include the borrower's good
standing, if the borrower is an entity, the financial condition of the
borrower, the due execution of the loan documents, the borrower's
ownership of the property and other similar matters.

After the representations, the borrower's obligations (referred to here a
"covenants") are listed, including the borrower's agreement to construct the
project, if the loan is a construction loan. Here is an example:

Borrower agrees and covenants with Lender as follows:

A.  Construction and Completion of Project. To

construct and develop the Project continually and with due diligence in

compliance with the Plans and Specifications and applicable law so as to

complete the same, in usable condition with full certificates of occupancy

and all other required licenses, permits and public approvals issued, on or

before the Completion Date.

Among the important covenants to focus on when reviewing or drafting a
loan agreement are the financial covenants, including any requirements that
the borrower maintain a required financial condition and produce various
financial documents. Here is an example of the former:

Electronic copy available at: https://ssrn.com/abstract=4294001
           H. Debt Coverage Ratio. The Borrower shall maintain (i) a
 Debt Coverage Ratio for the Loan of at least 110%, and (ii) a Debt
 Coverage Ratio for All Debt of at least 105%. A Debt Coverage Ratio for
 All Debt means the ratio calculated by dividing the Net Operating Income
 for any period by the scheduled debt service for all debt on the Mortgaged
 Property that requires current debt service, including the Loan, for such
 period. The Debt Coverage Ratio for the Loan means the ratio calculated
 by dividing the Net Operating Income for any period by the scheduled
 debt service for the Loan for such period. The Net Operating Income
 means, for any period, the difference between the Project's actual rental
 receipts received during such period less the sum of (x) Operating
 Expenses paid or accrued during such period plus (y) scheduled deposits
 to the Replacement Reserve Account for such period.

As you can see, this covenant incorporates a number of detailed definitions
that have to be reviewed to fully understand what is required. Financial
reporting covenants are also important to review carefully. Here is an
example of a reporting requirement:

 H. Financial Reporting. The Borrower shall furnish the Lender with
 such reports, financial statements, records and other information relating
 to the financial condition or operations of the Borrower and the
 construction and operation of the Project and as the Lender may
 reasonably require, including, but not limited to, (i) annual audited
 financial statements of the Borrower (to be delivered to the Lender within
 one hundred twenty (120) days of the end of Borrower's fiscal year), and
 (iii) such other reports to show that the Project is being built and operated
 consistently with this Agreement, the organizational documents of the
 Borrower, and the Loan Documents.

In addition to the financial covenants, the loan agreement may also provide
for the creation of various reserve and deposit accounts; and the funds in
those accounts may be used to pay for insurance and taxes or maintenance
expenses, or the account may be an operating account used for the
disbursement of loan proceeds, as in this example:

                          Electronic copy available at: https://ssrn.com/abstract=4294001
(g) Borrower shall maintain with Bank throughout the term of the Loan,
    and any extension thereof, an interest bearing commercial operating
    account ("Operating Account"). All disbursements of Loan proceeds
    may be made by the Bank by crediting such disbursements directly
    into the Operating Account. Borrower agrees that such disbursements
    shall constitute Advances under this Agreement and the Note. In
    addition, Borrower authorizes Bank to pay any principal or interest
    upon the Note when and as the same shall become due under the terms
    thereof by debiting the Operating Account.

The next section in a loan agreement usually lists the "Events of Default"
and the Lender's remedies in the event any of those Events occur. A
"default" is a breach of the agreement. An "Event of Default" is a breach of
the agreement that continues beyond a prescribed period after notice of is
given. If an "Event of Default" occurs the lender usually has the right
declare the entire loan amount immediately due and payable (i.e. the lender
has the right to "accelerate" the loan). Here are excerpts from two
applicable provisions in a loan agreement:

SECTION 7.     EVENTS OF DEFAULT

       The occurrence of any one or more of the following events
constitutes an "Event of Default" under the terms of this Agreement:

*           *  *

       7.3 The Borrower fails to pay the principal of, or fees, or interest
on, the Note or any other indebtedness of the Borrower under the Loan
Documents after the same is due and payable and such failure continues
beyond the date which is ten (10) days after written demand is made by
the Lender.

            Electronic copy available at: https://ssrn.com/abstract=4294001
       7.4 The Borrower defaults in the due observance or performance
of any other covenant, condition, or agreement to be observed or
performed by the Borrower pursuant to the terms of any of the Loan
Documents and such default remains uncured thirty (30) days after
written notice is given by the Lender to the Borrower.

SECTION 8.  RIGHTS ON DEFAULT

       Upon the occurrence of any one or more of the Events of Default
enumerated in the foregoing Section 7, and at any time thereafter, then:

       8.1 The Lender may declare all indebtedness due under the Note
and any and all other indebtedness of the Borrower to the Lender due
under the other Loan Documents or otherwise to be due and payable,
whether or not the indebtedness evidenced by the Note or the other Loan
Documents is otherwise due and payable and whether or not the Lender
has initiated any foreclosure or other action for the enforcement pursuant
to the provisions of the Loan Documents, whereupon all indebtedness due
under the Note and the other Loan Documents and any other such
indebtedness becomes immediately due and payable, both as to principal
and interest, without presentment, demand, protest, or notice of any kind,
all of which are expressly waived by the Borrower.

Like the other agreements discussed in prior chapters, a loan agreement
usually ends with various administrative provisions, a testimonium and
signature blocks for the borrower and the lender.

D. Real Estate Mortgage

The purpose of a mortgage is to give the lender a security interest in the
land and the buildings comprising the project. The core of a real estate
mortgage is the conveyance of the property by the borrower to the lender as

            Electronic copy available at: https://ssrn.com/abstract=4294001
security for the loan. The language typically used would, for example, be
as follows:

                The Mortgagor, FOR CONSIDERATION PAID, HEREBY
 CONVEYS, TRANSFERS, ASSIGNS, SETS-OVER AND GRANTS to
 the Mortgagee, with mortgage covenants, to secure the payment of
 ________________________ and 00/100 Dollars ($_______________),
 with interest and any other charges due thereon, payable as provided in
 Mortgagor's promissory note of even date (the "Note"), to secure the
 performance of all covenants and agreements contained herein, in the
 Note and in a loan agreement of even date between Mortgagor and
 Mortgagee (the "Loan Agreement"), and to secure the payment and
 performance of all other debts, covenants and agreements of or by
 Mortgagor to or for the benefit of Mortgagee now existing or hereafter
 arising while this mortgage is still undischarged of record, all of its right,
 title and interest in and to the land, with buildings and other
 improvements thereon, whether now existing or hereafter constructed or
 located, commonly known as and numbered
 _____________________________, _______________, as more
 particularly described in Exhibit A attached hereto, together with (i) any
 and all further or additional title, estate, interest or rights which may, at
 any time, be acquired by Mortgagor in and to such land and
 improvements, and (ii) all rents, issues, benefits and profits arising from
 the foregoing.

The Mortgagor is the borrower and the Mortgagee is the lender. After the
core obligation or covenant, various additional covenants regarding the use
and maintenance of the property (the lender's collateral) are included. If the
mortgage is granted in a state that permits non-judicial foreclosures, the
lender is also granted a "power of sale" (the power to sell the property and
payoff the debt if an Event of Default occurs). Like promissory notes,
mortgages are signed by the mortgagee (borrower) only.

After execution, a mortgage must be recorded at the appropriate office. In
Florida, mortgages are recorded with the clerk of the circuit court. Also,

                          Electronic copy available at: https://ssrn.com/abstract=4294001
because mortgages are recorded the mortgagor's signature must typically be
notarized and/or witnessed.

E. Security Agreement

The purpose of a security agreement is usually to give the lender a security
interest in personal property, like machinery and equipment or inventory (a
mortgage gives the lender a security interest in real property). In a real
estate deal, this would typically include an assignment of leases and rents.
Often the security agreement is incorporated in the mortgage, but it may
also be set forth in a separate document. Here is an example of the core
grant of a security interest in an assignment of leases and rents.

As further security for Borrower's payment and performance of the
Obligations, Borrower agrees with Lender as follows:

1.    Subject to the terms and conditions of this Assignment,

Borrower hereby transfers, assigns, and delivers to Lender as security for

Borrower's payment and performance of the Obligations all of

Borrower's right, title, and interest in and to:

(i)   All present and future leases, occupancy agreements, and

tenancies with respect to the Premises, together with all renewals,

extensions, and modifications thereof (collectively, "Leases");

(ii)  All rents and other payments due to Borrower by virtue of the

Leases or otherwise due to Borrower as the result of any use, possession,

or occupancy of any portion or portions of the Premises (collectively,

"Rents"); and

(iii) All right, title, and interest of Borrower in and to all guarantees
of the Leases.

The legal requirements for a security interest in personal property are
different than the requirements for a security interest in real property.
Security interests in personal property are governed by Article IX of the
Uniform Commercial Code. Article IX requires, among other things, that

               Electronic copy available at: https://ssrn.com/abstract=4294001
security interests in personal property be "perfected" by filing a separate
document called a "financing statement" with the appropriate filing office.
In Florida financing statements are filed in the Florida Transactions
Registry.
The legal requirements for creating a security interests in leases and rents
vary from state to state. It may be sufficient to file the assignment with the
mortgage or it may be necessary to file a separate financing statement. And
additional steps may be required as well, depending upon whatever state
law applies.
That is a quick outline of the documents involved in a commercial real
estate loan. And those are typical examples of the types of form documents
you often work with in a transactional practice. You probably noticed the
sample provisions I included contain some legalese and often don't conform
to the conventions discussed in chapters two through six of this book. The
primary reason for that is because the documents were drafted before law
schools started offering courses on contract drafting. If you get the
opportunity to revise the forms you are using, you can do better!

                          Electronic copy available at: https://ssrn.com/abstract=4294001

_____________________________________________________________

and interest, calculated at the fixed rate set forth below and the final

made on _________ ___, 20___, and the remainder of said payments are

20__.

         The interest on the unpaid balance shall be payable on the dates
provided above and is to be computed on the basis of a three hundred sixty
(360)day year and actual days elapsed as follows: at a variable rate per
year of _________________ (___) percentage points in excess of the
Base Rate (as defined in the Loan Agreement (the "Agreement") of even

Electronic copy available at: https://ssrn.com/abstract=4294001
date between the Borrower and the Bank) in effect from time to time at the
Bank.

         On default or after maturity or after judgment has been rendered on
this Note, the unpaid principal balance shall, at the option of the Bank, bear
interest at a rate which is three (3) percentage points per annum greater than
that which would otherwise be applicable. The Bank may collect a late
charge not to exceed six percent (6.00%) of any installment of interest or
principal, or of any other amount due to the Bank which is not paid or
reimbursed within fourteen (14) days of the due date thereof to defray the
extra cost and expense involved in handling such delinquent payment and
the increased risk of noncollection. The minimum late charge shall be
$25.00.

         If, at any time, the rate of interest, together with all amounts which
constitute interest and which are reserved, charged or taken by Bank as
compensation for fees, services or expenses incidental to the making,
negotiating or collection of the loan evidenced hereby, shall be deemed by
any competent court of law, governmental agency or tribunal to exceed the
maximum rate of interest permitted to be charged by the Bank to the
Borrower, then, during such time as such rate of interest would be deemed
excessive, that portion of each sum paid attributable to that portion of such
interest rate that exceeds the maximum rate of interest so permitted shall be
deemed a voluntary prepayment of principal.

         Borrower may prepay this Note in whole or in part, at any time,
without penalty or premium. Any such prepayment shall be credited in the
inverse order of their maturity and shall not affect the obligation to pay the
regular installments required hereunder.

         All payments and prepayments shall be applied first to the payment
of all interest on the unpaid principal of this Note and the balance on
account of the principal and all other amounts due under this Note, the
Agreement or any Related Agreement (as defined in the Agreement). The
Bank is authorized, but not required, to charge any amount due hereunder or
under the Agreement or any Related Agreement to any account of the
Borrower when and as it becomes due.

                          Electronic copy available at: https://ssrn.com/abstract=4294001
         Upon the happening of any Event of Default (as defined in the
Agreement), the entire indebtedness with accrued interest thereon due under
this Note, shall, at the option of the Bank, accelerate and become
immediately due and payable without demand or notice of any kind.
Failure to exercise such option shall not constitute a waiver of the right to
exercise the same in the event of any subsequent default.

         This Note has been executed and delivered in accordance with the
Agreement, incorporated herein by reference, which contains, among
others, terms and conditions upon which the entire unpaid principal hereof
and all interest hereon may become due and payable prior to the stated
maturity hereof and provisions as to further rights of the Bank and duties of
the Borrower and any Guarantor (as defined in the Agreement) with respect
hereto. This Note is secured by collateral as further described in certain of
the Related Agreements.

         The Borrower agrees to pay all taxes levied or assessed upon the
outstanding principal against any holder of this Note and to pay all costs,
including attorneys' fees and all other costs and expenses incurred in the
collection, protection, preservation, defense, administration or enforcement
of this Note or any guaranty or endorsement of this Note or in any litigation
arising out of the transactions of which this Note or any guaranty or
endorsement of this Note is a part.

         The Borrower hereby gives the Bank a lien and right of set off for
all of Borrower's liabilities and obligations upon and against all the
deposits, credits, collateral and property of the Borrower, now or hereafter
in the possession, custody, safekeeping or control of the Bank. At any time,
without demand or notice, Bank may set off the same or any part thereof
and apply the same to any liability or obligation of the Borrower even
though unmatured.

         THE BANK AND THE BORROWER IRREVOCABLY WAIVE
ALL RIGHT TO A TRIAL BY JURY IN ANY PROCEEDING
HEREAFTER INSTITUTED BY OR AGAINST THE BANK OR THE
BORROWER IN RESPECT OF THIS NOTE OR ARISING OUT OF
ANY DOCUMENT, INSTRUMENT OR AGREEMENT EVIDENCING,

                          Electronic copy available at: https://ssrn.com/abstract=4294001
GOVERNING OR SECURING THIS NOTE, INCLUDING THE
AFORESAID AGREEMENT.

         BORROWER (1) ACKNOWLEDGES THAT THE LOAN
EVIDENCED BY THIS NOTE IS PART OF A COMMERCIAL
TRANSACTION AND (2) TO THE EXTENT PERMITTED BY ANY
STATE OR FEDERAL LAW, WAIVES THE RIGHT BORROWER MAY
HAVE TO PRIOR NOTICE OF AND A HEARING ON THE RIGHT OF
ANY HOLDER OF THIS NOTE TO ANY REMEDY OR
COMBINATION OF REMEDIES THAT ENABLES SAID HOLDER, BY
WAY OF ATTACHMENT, FOREIGN ATTACHMENT, GARNISHMENT
OR REPLEVIN, TO DEPRIVE BORROWER OF ANY OF
BORROWER'S PROPERTY, AT ANY TIME, PRIOR TO FINAL
JUDGMENT IN ANY LITIGATION INSTITUTED IN CONNECTION
WITH THIS NOTE. The Borrower further waives diligence, demand,
presentment for payment, notice of nonpayment, protest and notice of
protest, and notice of any renewals or extensions of this Note, and all rights
under any statute of limitations, and agrees that the time for payment of this
Note may be changed and extended at Bank's sole discretion, without

all or any part of the security for the payment hereof at the discretion of
Bank, or the release of any party liable for this obligation without affecting
the liability of the other parties hereto. Any delay on the part of the Bank in
exercising any right hereunder shall not operate as a waiver of any such
right, and any waiver granted for one occasion shall not operate as a waiver

         This Note shall bind the heirs, executors, administrators, successors
and assigns of Borrower and shall inure to the benefit of the Bank, its
